</div>
<p><b>Guangzhou</b> (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hans">广州</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh-Hant">廣州</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>: <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">Guǎngzhōu</span></i> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Zh-Guangzhou.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Zh-Guangzhou.ogg" class="internal" title="Zh-Guangzhou.ogg">listen</a></span></span>); <a href="/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese" title="Yale romanization of Cantonese">Yale</a>: <i>Gwóngjāu</i>), <a href="/wiki/Postal_Map_Romanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Postal Map Romanization">historically</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Chinese" title="Romanization of Chinese">romanised</a> as <b>Canton</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_China" title="Provinces of China">Province</a> in southeastern China.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Located on the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> about 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) north-northwest of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and 145&#160;km (90&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, Guangzhou was a major terminus of the maritime <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and continues to serve as a major <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Guangzhou" title="Port of Guangzhou">port</a> and transportation hub.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guangzhou is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Chinese cities">3rd-largest Chinese city</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>; holds <a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial">sub-provincial</a> administrative status;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and is one of China's six <a href="/wiki/National_Central_City" title="National Central City">National Central Cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2014 the city's administrative area was estimated to have a population of 13,080,500 and forms part of one of the most populous metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">agglomerations</a> on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>. Some estimates place the population of the built-up area of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta_Economic_Zone" title="Pearl River Delta Economic Zone">Pearl River Delta Mega City</a> as high as 44 million without the Hong Kong <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_China" title="Special administrative regions of China">SAR</a> and 54 million including it. Guangzhou is identified as a Beta+ <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">Global city</a>. In recent years, there has been a rapidly increasing number of foreign residents and illegal immigrants from the Middle East, Eastern Europe and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Africans_in_Guangzhou" title="Africans in Guangzhou">from Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-12">[12]</a></sup> This has led to it being dubbed the "Capital of the Third World."<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The migrant population from other provinces of China in Guangzhou was 40 percent of the city's total population in 2008. Most of them are rural migrants, and they speak only Mandarin. They have taken on many jobs that the local citizens are unwilling to do.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guangzhou was long the only Chinese port permitted for most foreign traders. The city proper fell to the British and was opened by the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>. It lost trade to other ports such as <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, but continued to serve as a major entrepôt. In modern commerce, Guangzhou is best known for its annual <a href="/wiki/Canton_Fair" title="Canton Fair">Canton Fair</a>, the oldest, highest-level, largest-scale and most complete <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fair</a> in China. For the three consecutive years 2013–2015, Forbes ranked Guangzhou as the best commercial city on the Chinese mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p><span id="Etymology"></span><span id="Toponymy"></span><span id="Name"></span></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg/200px-Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg" width="200" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg/300px-Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg/400px-Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="767" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wuxian_Xiadong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Qing_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Empire">Qing</a>-era portrait of the <a href="/wiki/Grotto_of_the_Five_Immortals" class="mw-redirect" title="Grotto of the Five Immortals">Grotto of the Five Immortals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoist</a> temple around the five stones which gave Guangzhou its nickname "City of Rams".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Guǎngzhōu</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Chinese" title="Romanization of Chinese">romanisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> name <span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BB%A3%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:廣州">廣州</a></span>, which was <a href="/wiki/Simplified_characters" class="mw-redirect" title="Simplified characters">simplified</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> to <span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:广州">广州</a></span> in the 1950s. This name originally referred to the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial China">Imperial Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Guang_Prefecture_(Guangdong)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guang Prefecture (Guangdong)">Guang Prefecture</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_character" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese character">character</a> <span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BB%A3" class="extiw" title="wikt:廣">廣</a></span> or <span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF" class="extiw" title="wikt:广">广</a></span>—which also appears in the names <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liangguang" title="Liangguang">Liangguang</a>—means "broad" or "expansive" and refers to the valley of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> in comparison with the hill country of <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a> by which it was reached by the Chinese. In common with many other Chinese cities, including <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fuzhou" title="Fuzhou">Fuzhou</a>, the seat of the prefecture's government eventually took on its name. It became the municipality's formal designation on 15 February 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-swaymay_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swaymay-16">[16]</a></sup> It is sometimes abbreviated as GZ.</p>
<p>Before the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Zhou_(country_subdivision)" title="Zhou (country subdivision)">prefecture</a>, the town was known as <b>Panyu</b>, a name still borne by <a href="/wiki/Panyu_District" title="Panyu District">one of Guangzhou's districts</a> in the hinterlands. The origin of the name is still uncertain, with 11 various explanations being offered,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> including that it may have referred to two local mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The city has also sometimes been known as Guangzhou&#160;Fu or <b>Guangfu</b> after its status as the capital of a <a href="/wiki/Fu_(country_subdivision)" title="Fu (country subdivision)">commandery</a>. From this latter name, Guangzhou was known to medieval Arabs such as <a href="/wiki/Al-Masudi" title="Al-Masudi">Al-Masudi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khordadbeh" title="Ibn Khordadbeh">Ibn Khordadbeh</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> as <b>Khanfu</b> (<span lang="ar">خانفو</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Han" title="Southern Han">Southern Han</a>, the city was renamed <b>Xingwang</b>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing</a>, it was also known to its inhabitants as simply "The Provincial Capital".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_abbreviation" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese abbreviation">Chinese abbreviation</a> for Guangzhou is <b><span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%A9%97" class="extiw" title="wikt:穗">穗</a></span></b>, after its nickname "Rice City". As late as the early 20th century, most of the city continued to be made up of <a href="/wiki/Rice_paddies" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice paddies">rice paddies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27Time_Out.27.272011.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DmU31AgAAQBAJ.26pg.3DPA292_292.5D_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27Time_Out.27.272011.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DmU31AgAAQBAJ.26pg.3DPA292_292.5D-25">[25]</a></sup> The city has long borne the nickname <span class="nowrap"><b>City of Rams</b></span> or <span class="nowrap"><b>City of the Five Rams</b></span> from the five stones at the old <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Five_Immortals_(Guangzhou)" title="Temple of the Five Immortals (Guangzhou)">Temple of the Five Immortals</a> said to have been the sheep or goats ridden by the <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoist</a> <a href="/wiki/Culture_hero" title="Culture hero">culture heroes</a> credited with introducing <a href="/wiki/Rice_cultivation" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice cultivation">rice cultivation</a> to the area around the time of the city's foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The former name "City of the <a href="/wiki/Taoist_Immortal" class="mw-redirect" title="Taoist Immortal">Immortals</a>" came from the same story. The more recent <span class="nowrap"><b>City of Flowers</b></span> is usually taken as a simple reference to the area's greenery.</p>
<p>The former name "Canton" derived from <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> <i><span lang="pt">Cantão</span></i><sup id="cite_ref-hj_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hj-27">[27]</a></sup> or <i><span lang="pt">Ciudad de Cantão</span></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> a muddling of <a href="/wiki/Dialects_of_Chinese" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialects of Chinese">dialectical</a> pronunciations of "<a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Hakka" class="mw-redirect" title="Hakka">Hakka</a> <i>Kóng-tûng</i>). Although it originally and chiefly applied to the walled city, it was also used in English in reference to Guangdong generally.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> It was adopted as the <a href="/wiki/Postal_Map_Romanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Postal Map Romanization">Postal Map Romanization</a> of Guangzhou and remained in common use until the gradual adoption of <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>. As an adjective, it is still used in describing the <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese language">language</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese culture">culture</a> of Guangzhou and Guangdong. The 19th-century name "<span class="nowrap">Kwang-chow Foo</span>"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> derived from Nanjing Mandarin and the town's status as a <a href="/wiki/Fu_(administrative_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fu (administrative subdivision)">prefectural</a> capital.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Guangzhou" title="Timeline of Guangzhou">Timeline of Guangzhou</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A settlement now known as Nanwucheng was present in the area by <span class="nowrap">1100 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Some traditional Chinese histories placed Nanwucheng's founding during the reign of <a href="/wiki/King_Nan_of_Zhou" title="King Nan of Zhou">Ji Yan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-anatomy_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anatomy-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acc_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acc-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Zhou_emperors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Zhou emperors">king</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhou Dynasty">Zhou</a> from 314–256 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>. It was said to have consisted of little more than a stockade of bamboo and mud.<sup id="cite_ref-anatomy_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anatomy-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acc_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acc-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG/200px-Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG/300px-Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG/400px-Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Si_l%C3%BC_yu_yi.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Jade_burial_suit" title="Jade burial suit">jade burial suit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Mo" title="Zhao Mo">Zhao Mo</a> in Guangzhou's <a href="/wiki/Nanyue_King_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Nanyue King Museum">Nanyue King Museum</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanyue">Nanyue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Nanyue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Panyu was established on the east bank of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> in 214&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> to serve as a base for the <a href="/wiki/Qin_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Qin Empire">Qin Empire</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Qin_conquest_of_Guangdong" class="mw-redirect" title="Qin conquest of Guangdong">first failed invasion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Baiyue" title="Baiyue">Baiyue</a> lands in southern China. Legendary accounts claimed the soldiers at Panyu were so vigilant that they did not remove their armor for three years.<a href="#CITEREFGray1875">Gray (1875)</a>, p.&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com.hk/books?id=gi4NAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA3">3</a> Upon the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Qin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Qin">fall of the Qin</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Tuo" title="Zhao Tuo">Zhao Tuo</a> established his own kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Nanyue" title="Nanyue">Nanyue</a> and made Panyu its capital in 204&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>. It remained independent through the <a href="/wiki/Chu-Han_Contention" class="mw-redirect" title="Chu-Han Contention">Chu-Han Contention</a>, although Zhao negotiated recognition of his independence in exchange for his nominal submission to the <a href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Han Dynasty">Han</a> in 196&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-37">[37]</a></sup> Archaeological evidence shows that Panyu was an expansive commercial centre: in addition to items from central China, archaeologists have found remains originating from <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, India, and even <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Upon <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Yingqi" title="Zhao Yingqi">Zhao Yingqi</a>'s death in <span class="nowrap">115 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></span>, his younger son <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Xing" title="Zhao Xing">Zhao Xing</a> was named as his successor in violation of Chinese <a href="/wiki/Primogeniture" title="Primogeniture">primogeniture</a>. By <span class="nowrap">113 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></span>, his <a href="/wiki/Han_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Han people">Chinese</a> mother, the <a href="/wiki/Empress_dowager" title="Empress dowager">Empress Dowager</a> Jiu (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%A8%9B" class="extiw" title="wikt:樛">樛</a></span>) had prevailed upon him to submit Nanyue as a formal part of the Han Empire. The native <a href="/wiki/Grand_councilor" title="Grand councilor">prime minister</a> Lü Jia (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%91%82" class="extiw" title="wikt:呂">呂</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%98%89" class="extiw" title="wikt:嘉">嘉</a></span>) launched a coup, killing Han ambassadors along with the king, his mother, and their supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEY.C3.BC1987453_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEY.C3.BC1987453-39">[39]</a></sup> A successful ambush then annihilated a Han force which had been sent to arrest him. The enraged <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Han" title="Emperor Wu of Han">Emperor Wu</a> launched <a href="/wiki/Han%E2%80%93Nanyue_War" title="Han–Nanyue War">a massive river- and sea-borne invasion</a>: six armies under <a href="/wiki/Lu_Bode" title="Lu Bode">Lu Bode</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yang_Pu_(Western_Han)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yang Pu (Western Han) (page does not exist)">Yang Pu</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> took Panyu and annexed Nanyue by the end of 111&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEY.C3.BC1987453_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEY.C3.BC1987453-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_China">Imperial China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Imperial China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pearl_River_Yujitu.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pearl_River_Yujitu.png/200px-Pearl_River_Yujitu.png" width="200" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pearl_River_Yujitu.png/300px-Pearl_River_Yujitu.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pearl_River_Yujitu.png/400px-Pearl_River_Yujitu.png 2x" data-file-width="693" data-file-height="849" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

Guangzhou (as <span lang="zh">廣</span>) on the 1136 <a href="/wiki/Yuji_Tu" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuji Tu">Map of the Tracks of Yu</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_factories.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canton_factories.jpg/200px-Canton_factories.jpg" width="200" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canton_factories.jpg/300px-Canton_factories.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canton_factories.jpg/400px-Canton_factories.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1219" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Factories" title="Thirteen Factories">Thirteen Factories</a> c.<span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1805</span>, displaying the flags of <a href="/wiki/Denmark-Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Denmark-Norway">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Spain</a>, the United States, Sweden, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Flag" title="Prince's Flag">Netherlands</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_River,_26_May_1841.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg/200px-Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg" width="200" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg/300px-Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg/400px-Canton_River%2C_26_May_1841.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2629" data-file-height="1511" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canton_River,_26_May_1841.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guangzhou ("Canton") and the surrounding islands of <a href="/wiki/Henan_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Henan Island">Henan</a> ("Hanan"), <a href="/wiki/Pazhou" title="Pazhou">Pazhou</a> ("Whampoa"), <a href="/wiki/Changzhou_Island" title="Changzhou Island">Changzhou</a> ("Dane's Island"), and <a href="/wiki/Xiaoguwei" title="Xiaoguwei">Xiaoguwei</a> ("French Island") during the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Canton_(May_1841)" title="Battle of Canton (May 1841)">Second Battle of Canton</a>. The large <a href="/wiki/East_Indiamen" class="mw-redirect" title="East Indiamen">East Indiamen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Canton_System" title="Canton System">Canton trade</a> used <a href="/wiki/Pazhou#Anchorage" title="Pazhou">the anchorage</a> sheltered by these four islands, but the village and island of Huangpu for which it was named make up no part of present-day Guangzhou's <a href="/wiki/Huangpu_District,_Guangzhou" title="Huangpu District, Guangzhou">Huangpu District</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Western_Han_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Han dynasty">Han Empire</a>, Panyu became a provincial capital. In <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;226, it became the seat of Guang <a href="/wiki/Zhou_(country_subdivision)" title="Zhou (country subdivision)">Prefecture</a>, which gave it its modern name. The <i><a href="/wiki/Old_Book_of_Tang" title="Old Book of Tang">Old Book of Tang</a></i> described Guangzhou as important port in southern China.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Direct routes connected the Middle East and China, as shown in records of a Chinese prisoner returning home from Iraq twelve years after his capture at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Talas" title="Battle of Talas">Talas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Relations were not always peaceful: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Muslims</a> sacked the city on 30 October 758<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[n 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bret_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bret-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-welsh_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welsh-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-need_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-need-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sima_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sima-47">[46]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou massacre">were massacred</a> by the Chinese rebel <a href="/wiki/Huang_Chao" title="Huang Chao">Huang Chao</a> in 878, along with the city's <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in China">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christians_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Christians in China">Christians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-frenchy_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchy-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kaifung_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaifung-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gibberish_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gibberish-50">[49]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sirafi_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sirafi-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guy_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guy-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amid the <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms">Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms</a> that followed the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Later_Liang_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Liang (Five Dynasties)">Later Liang</a> governor <a href="/wiki/Liu_Yan_(emperor)" title="Liu Yan (emperor)">Liu Yan</a> used his base at Panyu to establish a "Great Yue" or "<a href="/wiki/Southern_Han" title="Southern Han">Southern Han</a>" empire, which lasted from 917 to 971. The region enjoyed considerable cultural and economic success in this period. From the 10th to 12th century, there are records that the large foreign communities were not exclusively male, but included "<a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persian</a> women".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[n 2]</a></sup> Guangzhou was visited by the <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccan</a> traveler <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Battuta" title="Ibn Battuta">Ibn Battuta</a> during his 14th-century journey around the world;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunn2005259_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunn2005259-57">[55]</a></sup> he detailed the process by which the Chinese constructed their large ships in the port's shipyards.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Hongwu_Emperor" title="Hongwu Emperor">Hongwu Emperor</a>'s declaration of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a>, he reversed his earlier support of foreign trade and imposed the first of a series of <a href="/wiki/Haijin" title="Haijin">sea bans</a> (<i>haijin</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA90_90.5D_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA90_90.5D-59">[57]</a></sup> These banned private foreign trade upon penalty of death for the merchant and exile for his family and neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELi2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DsrGEMarSWLYC.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELi2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DsrGEMarSWLYC.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D-60">[58]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan-era</a> maritime intendancies of Guangzhou, <a href="/wiki/Quanzhou" title="Quanzhou">Quanzhou</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ningbo" title="Ningbo">Ningbo</a> were closed in 1384<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA116_116.5D_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA116_116.5D-61">[59]</a></sup> and legal trade became limited to the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chinese_tributary_system" title="Imperial Chinese tributary system">tribute delegations</a> sent to or by official representatives of foreign governments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVon_Glahn1996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DDNlv4f9tV_AC.26pg.3DPA91_91.5D-62">[60]</a></sup> The policies exacerbated <a href="/wiki/Wokou" title="Wokou">"Japanese" pirate</a> attacks in the area until their removal in 1567.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Malacca_(1511)" title="Capture of Malacca (1511)">conquest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">Malacca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Perestrello" title="Rafael Perestrello">Rafael Perestrello</a> travelled to Guangzhou as a passenger on a native <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">junk</a> in 1516.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27Knight.27s.27.271841.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DZJteAAAAcAAJ.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27Knight.27s.27.271841.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DZJteAAAAcAAJ.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D-63">[61]</a></sup> His report induced <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Fernão Pires de Andrade">Fernão Pires de Andrade</a> to sail to the city with eight ships the next year,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27Knight.27s.27.271841.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DZJteAAAAcAAJ.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27Knight.27s.27.271841.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.hk.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DZJteAAAAcAAJ.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D-63">[61]</a></sup> but De Andrade's exploration<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR34_xxxiv.5D_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR34_xxxiv.5D-64">[62]</a></sup> was understood as spying<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998331_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998331-65">[63]</a></sup> and his brother <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sim%C3%A3o_de_Andrade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Simão de Andrade (page does not exist)">Simão</a> and others began attempting to monopolize trade,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998331.E2.80.932_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998331.E2.80.932-66">[64]</a></sup> enslaving Chinese women<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglas200611_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglas200611-67">[65]</a></sup> and children,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[n 3]</a></sup> engaging in piracy,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDutra_.26_al.1995426_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDutra_.26_al.1995426-70">[67]</a></sup> and fortifying the island of <a href="/wiki/Tam%C3%A3o" title="Tamão">Tamão</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998337.E2.80.938_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998337.E2.80.938-71">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR37_xxxvii.5D_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR37_xxxvii.5D-72">[69]</a></sup> Rumors even circulated that Portuguese were eating the children.<sup id="cite_ref-sjay_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sjay-73">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills_.26_al.2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DzERymZzBQQYC.26pg.3DPA28_28.5D_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills_.26_al.2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DzERymZzBQQYC.26pg.3DPA28_28.5D-68">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[n 4]</a></sup> The Guangzhou administration was charged with driving them off:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDutra_.26_al.1995426_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDutra_.26_al.1995426-70">[67]</a></sup> they bested the Portuguese at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tunmen" title="Battle of Tunmen">Battle of Tunmen</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998339_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998339-76">[72]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Xicaowan" title="Battle of Xicaowan">Xicao Bay</a>; held a <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A9_Pires" title="Tomé Pires">diplomatic mission</a> hostage in a failed attempt to pressure the restoration of the <a href="/wiki/Mahmud_Shah_of_Malacca" title="Mahmud Shah of Malacca">sultan of Malacca</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR40_xl.2C_xliii.5D_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR40_xl.2C_xliii.5D-77">[73]</a></sup> who had been accounted <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chinese_tributary_system" title="Imperial Chinese tributary system">a Ming vassal</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998340_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998340-78">[74]</a></sup> and, after placing them in <a href="/wiki/Cangue" title="Cangue">cangues</a> and keeping them for most of a year, ultimately executed 23 by <a href="/wiki/Lingchi" title="Lingchi">lingchi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR44_xliv.E2.80.93v.5D_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR44_xliv.E2.80.93v.5D-79">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[n 5]</a></sup> With the help of local pirates,<sup id="cite_ref-sjay_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sjay-73">[70]</a></sup> the "<a href="/wiki/Folangji" class="mw-redirect" title="Folangji">Folangji</a>" then carried out smuggling at <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macao" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Macao">Macao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lampacau" title="Lampacau">Lampacau</a>, and <span class="nowrap">St John's</span> Island (now <a href="/wiki/Shangchuan_Island" title="Shangchuan Island">Shangchuan</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDouglas200611_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDouglas200611-67">[65]</a></sup> until <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonel_de_Sousa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leonel de Sousa (page does not exist)">Leonel de Sousa</a> legalized their trade with bribes to Admiral <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wang_Bo_(admiral)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wang Bo (admiral) (page does not exist)">Wang Bo</a> (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B1%AA" class="extiw" title="wikt:汪">汪</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9F%8F" class="extiw" title="wikt:柏">柏</a></span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Luso-Chinese_agreement_(1554)" title="Luso-Chinese agreement (1554)">1554 Luso-Chinese Accord</a>. The Portuguese undertook not to raise fortifications and to pay customs dues;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWillis1998.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DtVhvh6ibLJcC.26pg.3DPA343_343.5D_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWillis1998.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DtVhvh6ibLJcC.26pg.3DPA343_343.5D-83">[78]</a></sup> three years later, after providing the Chinese with assistance suppressing their former pirate allies,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills1998343.E2.80.93344_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills1998343.E2.80.93344-84">[79]</a></sup> the Portuguese were permitted to warehouse their goods at <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Macau" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial Macau">Macau</a> instead of Guangzhou itself.<sup id="cite_ref-heyporter_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heyporter-85">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Qing_conquest_of_the_Ming#The_Southern_Ming" title="Qing conquest of the Ming">the fall</a> of <a href="/wiki/Fuzhou" title="Fuzhou">Fuzhou</a> in October 1646, the <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Yujian" title="Zhu Yujian">Longwu Emperor</a>'s brother <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Yuyue" title="Zhu Yuyue">Zhu Yuyue</a> fled by sea to Guangzhou. On 11 December, he declared himself the Shaowu Emperor, borrowing his imperial regalia from local theatre troupes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWakeman1985737_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWakeman1985737-86">[81]</a></sup> He led a successful offense against his cousin <a href="/wiki/Zhu_Youlang" title="Zhu Youlang">Zhu Youlang</a> but was deposed and executed on 20 January 1647 when the Ming turncoat <a href="/w/index.php?title=Li_Chengdong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Li Chengdong (page does not exist)">Li Chengdong</a> (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9D%8E" class="extiw" title="wikt:李">李</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%88%90" class="extiw" title="wikt:成">成</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9D%B1" class="extiw" title="wikt:東">東</a></span>) sacked the city on behalf of the Qing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWakeman1985738_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWakeman1985738-87">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[n 6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Qing became somewhat more open to foreign trade after gaining control of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tungning" title="Kingdom of Tungning">Taiwan</a> in 1683.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerdue2009_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerdue2009-89">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> from <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Macau" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial Macau">Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spaniards</a> from <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Philippines">Manila</a> returned, as did private Muslim, <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> traders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D-90">[84]</a></sup> From 1699 to 1714, the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">British East India Companies</a> sent a ship or two each year;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D-90">[84]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Ostend_Company" title="Ostend Company">Ostend General India Co.</a> arrived in 1717,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButel1997197_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButel1997197-91">[85]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Co.</a> in 1729,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[86]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Norway-Denmark" class="mw-redirect" title="Norway-Denmark">Danish</a> <a href="/wiki/Danish_Asiatic_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Asiatic Company">Asiatic Co.</a> in 1731,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[n 7]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Sweden">Swedish</a> <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">East India Co.</a> the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D-90">[84]</a></sup> These were joined by the occasional <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trieste_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Trieste Company">Trieste Company</a> vessel. The first independent American ship arrived in 1784 and the first <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial Australia">colonial Australian</a> one in 1788.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By that time, Guangzhou was one of the world's great ports, organised under the <a href="/wiki/Canton_System" title="Canton System">Canton System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKjellberg197599_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKjellberg197599-95">[88]</a></sup> The main exports were <a href="/wiki/History_of_tea" title="History of tea">tea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_porcelain" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese porcelain">porcelain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D_90-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D-90">[84]</a></sup> As a meeting place of merchants from all over the world, Guangzhou became a major contributor to the rise of the modern global economy.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 19th century, most of the city's buildings were still only one or two storeys. The major structures were the <a href="/wiki/Guangta" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangta">Plain Minaret</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Huaisheng_Mosque" title="Huaisheng Mosque">Huaisheng Mosque</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Flower_Pagoda" class="mw-redirect" title="Flower Pagoda">Flower Pagoda</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Six_Banyan_Trees" title="Temple of the Six Banyan Trees">Temple of the Six Banyan Trees</a>, and the guard tower known as the <a href="/wiki/Zhenhai_Tower_(Guangzhou)" title="Zhenhai Tower (Guangzhou)">5-Storey Pagoda</a>. The northern hills, since urbanized, were bare and covered with traditional graves. The brick city walls were about 6 miles (10&#160;km) in circumference, 25 feet (8&#160;m) high, and 20 feet (6&#160;m) wide. Its eight main gates and two water gates all held guards during the day and were closed at night. The wall rose to incorporate a hill on its northern side and was surrounded on the other three by a moat which, along with the canals, functioned as the city's sewer, emptied daily by the river's tides. A partition wall with four gates divided the northern "old town" from the southern "new town" closer to the river; the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Xiguan" title="Xiguan">Xiguan</a> ("West Gate") stretched beyond and the boats of fishers, traders, and <a href="/wiki/Tanka_people" title="Tanka people">Tanka</a> ("boat people") almost entirely concealed the riverbank for about 4 miles (6&#160;km). It was common for homes to have a storefront facing the street and to treat their <a href="/wiki/Chinese_courtyard_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese courtyard house">courtyards</a> as a kind of warehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> The city was part of a network of signal towers so effective that messages could be relayed to <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>—about 1,200 miles (1,931&#160;km) away—in less than 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKjellberg197595_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKjellberg197595-97">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Canton System was maintained until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a> in 1839. Following a series of battles in the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a>, the British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Canton_(March_1841)" title="Battle of Canton (March 1841)">captured Guangzhou itself</a> on 18 March 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27Bulletins_.26c..27.271841357_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27Bulletins_.26c..27.271841357-98">[91]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Canton_(May_1841)" title="Battle of Canton (May 1841)">Second Battle of Canton</a> was fought two months later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacPherson1843312_.26_315_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacPherson1843312_.26_315-99">[92]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Empire">Qing Empire</a>'s 1842 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">treaty</a> with <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a>, Guangzhou lost its privileged trade status as more and more <a href="/wiki/Treaty_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty port">treaty ports</a> were opened to more and more countries, usually including extraterritorial enclaves. Amid the decline of Qing prestige and the chaos of the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping Rebellion</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Punti" title="Punti">Punti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hakka_people" title="Hakka people">Hakka</a> waged <a href="/wiki/Punti-Hakka_Clan_Wars" title="Punti-Hakka Clan Wars">a series of clan wars</a> from 1855 to 1867. The <a href="/wiki/Third_plague_pandemic" title="Third plague pandemic">third pandemic</a> of <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> reached Guangzhou in 1894 and caused the death of 60,000 people in a few weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>The concession for the <a href="/wiki/Canton%E2%80%93Hankow_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton–Hankow Railway">Canton–Hankow Railway</a> was awarded to the <a href="/wiki/American_China_Development_Company" title="American China Development Company">American China Development Co.</a> in 1898. It completed <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Sanshui_Railway" title="Guangzhou–Sanshui Railway">its branch line</a> west to <a href="/wiki/Foshan" title="Foshan">Foshan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanshui" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanshui">Sanshui</a> before being engulfed in a diplomatic crisis after a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Belgium">Belgian</a> consortium bought a controlling interest and the Qing cancelled its concession. <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="J.P. Morgan">J.P. Morgan</a> was awarded millions in damages<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[94]</a></sup> and the line to <a href="/wiki/Wuchang_District" title="Wuchang District">Wuchang</a> wasn't completed until 1936<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[95]</a></sup> and a unified <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou_Railway" title="Beijing–Guangzhou Railway">Beijing–Guangzhou Railway</a> waited until the completion of <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_Yangtze_River_Bridge" title="Wuhan Yangtze River Bridge">Yangtze River Bridge</a> in 1957.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_China">Modern China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PLA_Troops_entered_to_Guangzhou.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Communist Party">Communist</a> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">troops</a> entering Guangzhou on 14 October 1949</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the late Qing, Guangzhou was the site of failed revolts in <a href="/wiki/First_Guangzhou_Uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="First Guangzhou Uprising">1895</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Guangzhou_Uprising" title="Second Guangzhou Uprising">1911</a>; the 72 identifiable bodies found after the latter are remembered as the city's 72 <a href="/wiki/Martyrdom_in_Chinese_culture" title="Martyrdom in Chinese culture">Martyrs</a> at Huanghuagang ("Yellow Flower Mound") Mausoleum. After the <a href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinhai Revolt">Xinhai Revolt</a> had overthrown the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing</a>, the assassination of <a href="/wiki/Song_Jiaoren" title="Song Jiaoren">Song Jiaoren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>'s attempts to remove <a href="/wiki/KMT" class="mw-redirect" title="KMT">Nationalists</a> from power; <a href="/wiki/Hu_Hanmin" title="Hu Hanmin">Hu Hanmin</a> joined the 1913 <a href="/wiki/Second_Revolution_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Revolution (China)">Second Revolution</a> against him<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[96]</a></sup> but was forced to flee to <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> after its failure. Upon Yuan's attempt to declare himself the Hongxian Emperor of <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_China_(1915%E2%80%9316)" title="Empire of China (1915–16)">China</a>, Guangdong <a href="/wiki/National_Protection_War" title="National Protection War">again revolted</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChan2009.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DBU4zLLh3M0oC.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChan2009.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DBU4zLLh3M0oC.26pg.3DPA135_135.5D-104">[97]</a></sup> and became effectively independent on 25 June 1917 with help from the naval commander at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup> In August, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a> established the Guangzhou Military Government as part of the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Protection_Movement" title="Constitutional Protection Movement">Constitutional Protection Movement</a>. It borrowed <a href="/wiki/Chinese_dollar" title="Chinese dollar">$</a>2,000,000 from the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> for its army and navy, then declared war on it on September 13.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup> The new <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912-1949)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China (1912-1949)">Republic of China</a> merged the eastern part of <a href="/wiki/Nanhai_County" title="Nanhai County">Nanhai County</a> and the northern part of <a href="/wiki/Panyu_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Panyu County">Panyu County</a> with Guangzhou in 1918 and established an urban council to govern it.<sup id="cite_ref-swaymay_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swaymay-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amid the <a href="/wiki/Warlord_Era" title="Warlord Era">Warlord Era</a>, the Guangzhou government was overwhelmed by <a href="/wiki/Lu_Rongting" title="Lu Rongting">Lu Rongting</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Old_Guangxi_Clique" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Guangxi Clique">Guangxi Clique</a>. Sun fled to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_International_Settlement" title="Shanghai International Settlement">Shanghai</a> in November 1918 until <a href="/wiki/Chen_Jiongming" title="Chen Jiongming">Chen Jiongming</a> restored him in October 1920 during the <a href="/wiki/Yuegui_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuegui Wars">Yuegui Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup> The name Guangzhou was made official the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-swaymay_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swaymay-16">[16]</a></sup> In January 1922, the Nationalists organized a major strike among the tens of thousands of dockworkers and sailors in Guangzhou and <a href="/wiki/British_Hong_Kong" title="British Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup> On 16 June, <a href="/wiki/Ye_Ju" title="Ye Ju">Ye Ju</a> assaulted <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall_(Guangzhou)" title="Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall (Guangzhou)">Guangzhou's presidential palace</a> after Chen and Sun differed over whether to accept an accommodation with the <a href="/wiki/Zhili_Clique" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhili Clique">Zhili Clique</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beiyang_government" title="Beiyang government">government</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>; Sun had already fled but <a href="/wiki/Soong_Ching-ling" title="Soong Ching-ling">his wife</a> narrowly escaped <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">shelling</a> and rifle fire before meeting him<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPakula2009.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D4ZpVntUTZfkC.26pg.3DPA95_95.E2.80.9397.5D_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPakula2009.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3D4ZpVntUTZfkC.26pg.3DPA95_95.E2.80.9397.5D-106">[99]</a></sup> on the gunboat <i><a href="/wiki/Zhongshan_(warship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhongshan (warship)">Yongfeng</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[100]</a></sup> under <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>. In autumn, Sun and his party raised more than 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_dollar" title="Chinese dollar">Chinese dollars</a> from supporters to recapture Guangzhou.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilbur1983.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DhHrQKIKvZK8C.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilbur1983.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DhHrQKIKvZK8C.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D-108">[101]</a></sup> Their mercenaries removed Chen on 15 January 1923, and he returned to the city on 21 February.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilbur_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilbur-109">[102]</a></sup> His armies were then kept in the field largely through tax levies collected through the city's efficient police force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilbur1983.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DhHrQKIKvZK8C.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilbur1983.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DhHrQKIKvZK8C.26pg.3DPA3_3.5D-108">[101]</a></sup> In December, he planned to seize Guangzhou's maritime customs duties but foreign gunboats led him to drop the plan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sun and Chiang used <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">Soviet</a> funds and weapons to develop the <a href="/wiki/Whampoa_Military_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Whampoa Military Academy">Whampoa Military Academy</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeck2007_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeck2007-105">[98]</a></sup> on <a href="/wiki/Changzhou_Island" title="Changzhou Island">Changzhou</a> from 1924 on. In August, they acted to confiscated weapons being purchased by the Canton Merchants' Volunteer Corps. This led to <a href="/wiki/Canton_Merchants%27_Corps_Uprising" title="Canton Merchants' Corps Uprising">rioting and a military stand-off</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Xiguan" title="Xiguan">western suburbs</a> from 10–15 October; its suppression damaged <a href="/wiki/Xiguan" title="Xiguan">Xiguan</a> with large fire. During Sun's life, his son <a href="/wiki/Sun_Fo" title="Sun Fo">Sun Fo</a> served as <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Guangzhou" title="Mayor of Guangzhou">mayor</a> of Guangzhou when he was in power from 1920 on; his role did not survive Sun's death by cancer in 1925. The "<a href="/wiki/Canton_Coup" title="Canton Coup">Canton Coup</a>" on 20 March 1926 saw Chiang solidify his control over the <a href="/wiki/KMT" class="mw-redirect" title="KMT">Nationalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army" title="National Revolutionary Army">their army</a> against <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei" title="Wang Jingwei">Wang Jingwei</a>, the party's left wing, its <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Communist Party">Communist</a> <a href="/wiki/First_United_Front" title="First United Front">allies</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">Soviet</a> advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[104]</a></sup> By May, he had ended civilian control of the military<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAh_Xiang19983_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAh_Xiang19983-112">[105]</a></sup> and begun his <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition_(1926%E2%80%931927)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Expedition (1926–1927)">Northern Expedition</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Warlord_Era" title="Warlord Era">warlords</a> of the north. Ultimately successful, it turned him into the country's paramount leader. <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> worked in the city, running the 6th term of the KMT's <a href="/wiki/Peasant_Movement_Training_Institute_at_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="Peasant Movement Training Institute at Guangzhou">Peasant Movement Training Institute</a> from May to September 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[107]</a></sup> In 1927, <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Fakui" title="Zhang Fakui">Zhang Fakui</a> recovered Guangzhou from the <a href="/wiki/New_Guangxi_Clique" class="mw-redirect" title="New Guangxi Clique">New Guangxi Clique</a>. Zhang's suppression of the 11 December <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Uprising" title="Guangzhou Uprising">Guangzhou Uprising</a> saw even greater numbers of Communists and suspect workers and students killed than at the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai Massacre">Shanghai Massacre</a> earlier in the year.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, following <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Bombing_During_World_War_II#Japanese_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic Bombing During World War II">its aerial bombardment</a>, Guangzhou was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> from 21 October 1938 to 16 September 1945. <a href="/wiki/Unit_8604" title="Unit 8604">Unit 8604</a>, a section of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Unit_731" title="Unit 731">Unit 731</a>, conducted bacteriological research in the city during the war. Amid the closing months of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, Guangzhou briefly served as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> after the fall of Nanjing in April 1949. The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">People's Liberation Army</a> entered the city on 14 October 1949. Amid a massive exodus to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Macau" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial Macau">Macau</a>, the <a href="/wiki/KMT" class="mw-redirect" title="KMT">Nationalists</a> blew up the <a href="/wiki/Haizhu_Bridge" title="Haizhu Bridge">Haizhu Bridge</a> across the Pearl River to protect the government's flight to <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> initiated building projects including new housing on the banks of the Pearl River to adjust the city's <a href="/wiki/Boat_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Boat people">boat people</a> to life on land. Since the 1980s, the city's close proximity to <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> and its ties to <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a> have made it one of the major beneficiaries of China's <a href="/wiki/Opening_up_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Opening up policy">opening up</a> under <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a>. Beneficial tax reforms in the 1990s have also helped the city's industrialisation and development.</p>
<p>The municipality was expanded in the year 2000, with <a href="/wiki/Huadu_District" title="Huadu District">Huadu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panyu_District" title="Panyu District">Panyu</a> joining the city as <a href="/wiki/District_(China)" title="District (China)">urban districts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conghua" class="mw-redirect" title="Conghua">Conghua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zengcheng" class="mw-redirect" title="Zengcheng">Zengcheng</a> as more rural <a href="/wiki/County_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="County (China)">counties</a>. The former districts of <a href="/wiki/Dongshan_District,_Guangzhou" title="Dongshan District, Guangzhou">Dongshan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fangcun_District" title="Fangcun District">Fangcun</a> were abolished in 2005, merged into <a href="/wiki/Yuexiu_District" title="Yuexiu District">Yuexiu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liwan_District" title="Liwan District">Liwan</a> respectively. They were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Nansha_District" title="Nansha District">Nansha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luogang_District" title="Luogang District">Luogang</a>. The former was carved out of <a href="/wiki/Panyu_District" title="Panyu District">Panyu</a>, the latter from parts of <a href="/wiki/Baiyun_District,_Guangzhou" title="Baiyun District, Guangzhou">Baiyun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tianhe_District" title="Tianhe District">Tianhe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zengcheng" class="mw-redirect" title="Zengcheng">Zengcheng</a>, and an exclave within <a href="/wiki/Huangpu_District,_Guangzhou" title="Huangpu District, Guangzhou">Huangpu</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_People%27s_Congress" title="National People's Congress">National People's Congress</a> approved a development plan for the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a> in January 2009; on March 19 the same year, the Guangzhou and <a href="/wiki/Foshan" title="Foshan">Foshan</a> municipal governments agreed to establish a framework to merge the two cities.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[108]</a></sup> In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Luogang_District" title="Luogang District">Luogang</a> merged into <a href="/wiki/Huangpu_District,_Guangzhou" title="Huangpu District, Guangzhou">Huangpu</a> and both <a href="/wiki/Conghua_District" title="Conghua District">Conghua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zengcheng_District" title="Zengcheng District">Zengcheng</a> counties were upgraded to districts. Guangzhou was then the most populous consolidated district-governed city in China until Beijing overtook it the next year.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tiantang_Peak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tiantang_Peak.jpg/220px-Tiantang_Peak.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tiantang_Peak.jpg/330px-Tiantang_Peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Tiantang_Peak.jpg/440px-Tiantang_Peak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tiantang_Peak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tiantang_Peak" title="Tiantang Peak">Tiantang Peak</a>, highest mountain in Guangzhou</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The old town of Guangzhou was near <a href="/wiki/Baiyun_Mountain" title="Baiyun Mountain">Baiyun Mountain</a> on the east bank of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> (Zhujiang) about 80 miles (129&#160;km) from its junction with the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> and about 300 miles (483&#160;km) below its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_navigation" title="Head of navigation">head of navigation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> It commanded the rich alluvial plain of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a>, with its connection to the sea protected at the <a href="/wiki/Humen_Strait" class="mw-redirect" title="Humen Strait">Humen Strait</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> The present city spans 7,434.4 square kilometres (2,870.4&#160;sq&#160;mi) on both sides of the river from <span class="nowrap">112° 57′</span> to <span class="nowrap">114° 03′ E</span> longitude and <span class="nowrap">22° 26′</span> to <span class="nowrap">23° 56′ N</span> latitude in south-central Guangdong. The Pearl is the <a href="/wiki/Rivers_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers of China">3rd-largest river</a> of China.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[111]</a></sup> Baiyun Mountain is now locally referred to as the city's "lung" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B8%82" class="extiw" title="wikt:市">市</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%82%BA" class="extiw" title="wikt:肺">肺</a></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-Official_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[112]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="(July 2016)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The elevation of the prefecture generally increases from southwest to northeast, with mountains forming the backbone of the city and the ocean comprising the front. <a href="/wiki/Tiantang_Peak" title="Tiantang Peak">Tiantang Peak</a> (<span lang="zh-hans">天堂顶</span>, "Heavenly Peak") is the highest point of elevation at 1,210 metres (3,970&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Located just south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>, Guangzhou has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cfa</i>) influenced by the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_monsoon" class="mw-redirect" title="East Asian monsoon">East Asian monsoon</a>. Summers are wet with high temperatures, high humidity, and a high <a href="/wiki/Heat_index" title="Heat index">heat index</a>. Winters are mild and comparatively dry. Guangzhou has a lengthy <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> season, spanning from April through September. Monthly averages range from 13.6&#160;°C (56.5&#160;°F) in January to 28.6&#160;°C (83.5&#160;°F) in July, while the annual mean is 22.6&#160;°C (72.7&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Official_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official-9">[9]</a></sup> Autumn, from October to December, is very moderate, cool and windy, and is the best travel time.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[113]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Humidity#Relative_humidity" title="Humidity">relative humidity</a> is approximately 68 percent, whereas <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">annual rainfall</a> in the metropolitan area is over 1,700&#160;mm (67&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-Official_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official-9">[9]</a></sup> With monthly percent possible sunshine ranging from 17 percent in March and April to 52 percent in November, the city receives 1,628 hours of bright sunshine annually, considerably less than nearby <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen#Climate" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong#Climate" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>. Extreme temperatures have ranged from 0&#160;°C (32&#160;°F) to 39.1&#160;°C (102.4&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Mherrera_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mherrera-121">[114]</a></sup> The last recorded snowfall in the city was on 24 January 2016, 87 years after the second last recorded snowfall.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p><br /></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_divisions_of_Guangzhou" title="List of administrative divisions of Guangzhou">List of administrative divisions of Guangzhou</a></div>
<p>Guangzhou is a <a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">sub-provincial city</a>. It has direct jurisdiction over eleven <a href="/wiki/District_(China)" title="District (China)">districts</a>:</p>

<p><span id="Guangzhou_International_Convention_and_Exhibition_Center"></span></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guangzhou_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Guangzhou_skyline.jpg/200px-Guangzhou_skyline.jpg" width="200" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Guangzhou_skyline.jpg/300px-Guangzhou_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Guangzhou_skyline.jpg/400px-Guangzhou_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="989" data-file-height="682" /></a>

<div class="thumb tright">
