<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1_guangzhou_shopping_2011.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shangxiajiu" class="mw-redirect" title="Shangxiajiu">Shangxiajiu</a> Pedestrian Street</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guangzhou is the main manufacturing hub of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>'s leading commercial and manufacturing regions. In 2013, the GDP reached ¥1542 billion (US$248 billion), per capita was ¥120,515 (US $19,459).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[121]</a></sup> Guangzhou is considered one of the most prosperous cities in China. But due to rapid industrialisation, it is also considered one of the most polluted cities.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Canton_Fair" title="Canton Fair">Canton Fair</a>, formally the "China Import and Export Fair", is held every year in April and October by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Trade_(China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Trade (China)">Ministry of Trade</a>. Inaugurated in the spring of 1957, the fair is a major event for the city. It is the <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fair</a> with the longest history, highest level, largest scale in China.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[122]</a></sup> From the 104th session onwards, the fair moved to the new <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_International_Convention_and_Exhibition_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou International Convention and Exhibition Center">Guangzhou International Convention and Exhibition Center</a> (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:广州">广州</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9B%BD%E9%99%85" class="extiw" title="wikt:国际">国际</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%BC%9A%E5%B1%95" class="extiw" title="wikt:会展">会展</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%B8%AD%E5%BF%83" class="extiw" title="wikt:中心">中心</a></span>) in <a href="/wiki/Pazhou" title="Pazhou">Pazhou</a>, from the older complex in Liuhua. The GICEC is served by two stations on <a href="/wiki/Line_8,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 8, Guangzhou Metro">Metro Line 8</a>. Since the 104th session, the Canton Fair has been arranged in three phases instead of two phases.</p>
<p>Guangzhou is one the largest hubs of China's <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade_in_China" title="Illegal drug trade in China">illegal drug trade</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_products">Local products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Local products">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(June 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cantonese_cuisine" title="Cantonese cuisine">Cantonese</a> is one of China's most famous and popular <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">regional cuisines</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Chengyu" title="Chengyu">saying</a> stating simply to "Eat in Guangzhou" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%A3%9F" class="extiw" title="wikt:食">食</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:在">在</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:广州">广州</a></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[n 8]</a></sup></li>
<li>Cantonese <a href="/wiki/Sculpture_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sculpture in China">sculpture</a> includes work in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_jade" title="Chinese jade">jade</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_wood_carving#Indochina_and_the_Far_East" title="History of wood carving">wood</a>, and (now <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_ivory" title="Destruction of ivory">controversially</a>) <a href="/wiki/Ivory_trade" title="Ivory trade">ivory</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canton_porcelain" title="Canton porcelain">Canton porcelain</a> developed over the past three centuries as one of the major forms of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_export_porcelain" title="Chinese export porcelain">exportware</a>. It is now known within China for its highly colorful style.</li>
<li>Cantonese embroidery is one of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_embroidery" title="Chinese embroidery">China's four main styles</a> of the art and is represented in Guangzhou, although its principal centre is at <a href="/wiki/Chaozhou" title="Chaozhou">Chaozhou</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhujiang_Beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhujiang Beer">Zhujiang Beer</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Pale_lager" title="Pale lager">pale lager</a>, is one of China's most successful brands. It is made in Guangzhou from water piped directly to the brewery from a natural spring.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_zones">Industrial zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Industrial zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Economic_and_Technological_Development_Zone" title="Guangzhou Economic and Technological Development Zone">Guangzhou Economic and Technological Development Zone</a></li>
<li>Guangzhou Nansha Export Processing Zone</li>
</ul>
<p>The Export Processing Zone was founded in 2005. Its total planned area is 1.36&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (0.53&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-rightsite1_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rightsite1-131">[123]</a></sup> It is located in Nansha District and it belongs to the provincial capital, Guangzhou. The major industries encouraged in the zone include automobile assembly, biotechnology and heavy industry. It is situated 54 kilometres (34 miles) (70 minutes drive) south of Guangzhou Baiyun International Airport and close to Nansha Port. It also has the advantage of Guangzhou Metro line 4 which is being extended to Nansha Ferry Terminal.</p>
<ul>
<li>Guangzhou Free Trade Zone</li>
</ul>
<p>The zone was founded in 1992. It is located in the east of <a href="/wiki/Huangpu_District,_Guangzhou" title="Huangpu District, Guangzhou">Huangpu District</a> and near to Guangzhou Economic and Technological Development Zone. It is also very close to Guangzhou Baiyun Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[124]</a></sup> The major industries encouraged in the zone include international trade, logistics, processing and computer software.</p>

</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_PRC_census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 PRC census">2010 census</a> found Guangzhou's population to be 12.78 million. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it was estimated at 13,080,500,<sup id="cite_ref-gzdaily2014_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gzdaily2014-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-statyb2012_136-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statyb2012-136">[128]</a></sup> with 11,264,800 urban residents.<sup id="cite_ref-gzannals2014_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gzannals2014-3">[3]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> is thus around 1,800 people per km². The built-up area of the Guangzhou proper connects directly to several other cities. The built-up area of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta_Economic_Zone" title="Pearl River Delta Economic Zone">Pearl River Delta Economic Zone</a> covers around 17,573 square kilometres (6,785&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has been estimated to house 44 million people, including Guangzhou's nine urban districts, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> (10.36m), <a href="/wiki/Dongguan" title="Dongguan">Dongguan</a> (8.22m), <a href="/wiki/Zhongshan" title="Zhongshan">Zhongshan</a> (3.12m), most of <a href="/wiki/Foshan" title="Foshan">Foshan</a> (7.2m), <a href="/wiki/Jiangmen" title="Jiangmen">Jiangmen</a> (1.82m), <a href="/wiki/Zhuhai" title="Zhuhai">Zhuhai</a> (890k), and <a href="/wiki/Huizhou" title="Huizhou">Huizhou</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Huiyang_District" title="Huiyang District">Huiyang District</a> (760k).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The total population of this agglomeration is over 54 million after including the population of the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Special_Administrative_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong Special Administrative Region">Hong Kong Special Administrative Region</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The area's fast-growing economy and high demand for labour has produced a huge "floating population" of <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers">migrant workers</a>. Up to 30 million migrants reside in the area least six months each year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2008, about 5 million of Guangzhou's permanent residents were <a href="/wiki/Hukou_system" title="Hukou system">hukouless</a> migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-cri_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cri-137">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most of Guangzhou's population is <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>. Most of the local <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">Cantonese people</a> speak <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a> as their first language,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[131]</a></sup> while most migrants speak forms of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cri_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cri-137">[129]</a></sup> In 2010, each language was the native tongue of roughly half of the city's population,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[132]</a></sup> although significant numbers speak <a href="/wiki/Dialects_of_Chinese" class="mw-redirect" title="Dialects of Chinese">other dialects</a> as well. As with elsewhere in the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hukou_system" title="Hukou system">household registration system</a> (<i>hukou</i>) limits migrants' access to residences, educational institutions, and other public benefits. In May 2014, legally-employed migrants in Guangzhou were permitted to receive a <i>hukou</i> card allowing them to marry and <a href="/wiki/One-child_policy" title="One-child policy">obtain permission for their pregnancies</a> in the city, rather than having to return to their official hometowns as previously.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTHukou_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTHukou-141">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historically, the Cantonese people have made up a sizeable part of the 19th- and 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Chinese_diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese diaspora">Chinese diaspora</a> and many <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a> have ties to Guangdong. This is particularly true in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans" title="Chinese Americans">United States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lai_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lai-142">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Canadians" title="Chinese Canadians">Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[135]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Australians" title="Chinese Australians">Australia</a>.</p>
<p>Demographically, the only significant immigration into China has been by <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">overseas Chinese</a>, but Guangzhou sees many foreign tourists, workers, and residents from the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_China#People_from_other_immigration_jurisdictions" title="Demographics of China">usual locations</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Americans_in_China" title="Americans in China">United States</a>. Notably, it is also home to thousands of <a href="/wiki/Africans_in_Guangzhou" title="Africans in Guangzhou">African expatriates</a>, including people from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="box-sizing: border-box; overflow: hidden; float:right; margin:1px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Metro" title="Guangzhou Metro">Guangzhou Metro</a></div>
<p>When the first line of the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Metro" title="Guangzhou Metro">Guangzhou Metro</a> opened in 1997, Guangzhou was the fourth city in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> to have an underground railway system, behind <a href="/wiki/Beijing_subway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beijing subway">Beijing</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tianjin_subway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tianjin subway (page does not exist)">Tianjin</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_subway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shanghai subway (page does not exist)">Shanghai</a>. Currently the metro network is made up of nine lines, covering a total length of 266&#160;km (165&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[136]</a></sup> A long-term plan is to make the city's metro system expand to over 500&#160;km (310&#160;mi) by 2020 with 15 lines in operation.</p>
<p>As of January 2016 the lines of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Metro" title="Guangzhou Metro">Guangzhou Metro</a> include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_1,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 1, Guangzhou Metro">Line 1</a>: <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_East_Railway_Station_(metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou East Railway Station (metro)">Guangzhou East Railway Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Xilang_Station" title="Xilang Station">Xilang Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 2, Guangzhou Metro">Line 2</a>: <a href="/wiki/Jiahewanggang_Station" title="Jiahewanggang Station">Jiahewanggang Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_South_Railway_Station" title="Guangzhou South Railway Station">Guangzhou South Railway Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_3,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 3, Guangzhou Metro">Line 3</a>
<ul>
<li>South route: <a href="/wiki/Tianhe_Coach_Terminal_Station" title="Tianhe Coach Terminal Station">Tianhe Coach Terminal Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Panyu_Square_Station" title="Panyu Square Station">Panyu Square Station</a> via <a href="/wiki/Tiyu_Xilu_Station" title="Tiyu Xilu Station">Tiyu Xilu Station</a></li>
<li>North route: <a href="/wiki/Airport_South_Station_(Guangzhou)" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport South Station (Guangzhou)">Airport South Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Tiyu_Xilu_Station" title="Tiyu Xilu Station">Tiyu Xilu Station</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_4,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 4, Guangzhou Metro">Line 4</a>: <a href="/wiki/Huangcun_Station" title="Huangcun Station">Huangcun Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Jinzhou_Station_(Guangzhou_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jinzhou Station (Guangzhou Metro)">Jinzhou Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_5,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 5, Guangzhou Metro">Line 5</a>: <a href="/wiki/Jiaokou_Station" title="Jiaokou Station">Jiaokou Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Wenchong_Station" title="Wenchong Station">Wenchong Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_6,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 6, Guangzhou Metro">Line 6</a>: <a href="/wiki/Xunfenggang_Station" title="Xunfenggang Station">Xunfenggang Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Changban_Station" title="Changban Station">Changban Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_8,_Guangzhou_Metro" title="Line 8, Guangzhou Metro">Line 8</a>: <a href="/wiki/Fenghuang_Xincun_Station" title="Fenghuang Xincun Station">Fenghuang Xincun Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Wanshengwei_Station" title="Wanshengwei Station">Wanshengwei Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangfo_Metro" title="Guangfo Metro">Guangfo Line</a>: <a href="/wiki/Yangang_Station" title="Yangang Station">Yangang Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Kuiqi_Lu_Station" title="Kuiqi Lu Station">Kuiqi Lu Station</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhujiang_New_Town_Automated_People_Mover_System" title="Zhujiang New Town Automated People Mover System">APM</a>: <a href="/wiki/Linhexi_Station" title="Linhexi Station">Linhexi Station</a>–<a href="/wiki/Canton_Tower_Station" title="Canton Tower Station">Canton Tower Station</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The first section of the Haizhu Tram line opened on 31 December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-trials_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trials-145">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motor_transport">Motor transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Motor transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bus_Routes_in_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Bus Routes in Guangzhou">List of Bus Routes in Guangzhou</a></div>
<p>In the 19th century, city already boasted over 600 long, straight streets; these were mostly paved but still very narrow.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Bus_Rapid_Transit" title="Guangzhou Bus Rapid Transit">Guangzhou Bus Rapid Transit</a> (GBRT) system which was introduced in 2010, is the world's 2nd-largest <a href="/wiki/Bus_Rapid_Transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Bus Rapid Transit">Bus Rapid Transit</a> system with 1,000,000 passenger trips daily<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[138]</a></sup> and 26,900 <a href="/wiki/Passengers_per_hour_per_direction" title="Passengers per hour per direction">pphpd</a> during the peak hour (second only to the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> BRT system in Bogota).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[139]</a></sup> The system averages 1 bus every 10 seconds or 350 per hour in a single direction and contains the world's longest BRT stations—around 260&#160;m (850&#160;ft) including bridges.</p>
<p>In 2009, it was reported that all 9,424 buses and 17,695 taxis in Guangzhou would be operating on <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">LPG</a>-fuel by 2010 to promote clean energy for transport and improve the environment ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Games" title="2010 Asian Games">2010 Asian Games</a> which were held in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[140]</a></sup> At present<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, Guangzhou is the city that uses the most LPG-fueled vehicles in the world, and at the end of 2006, 6,500 buses and 16,000 taxis were using LPG, taking up 85 percent of all buses and taxis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Effective January 1, 2007, the municipal government banned motorcycles in Guangdong's urban areas. Motorcycles found violating the ban are confiscated.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[141]</a></sup> The Guangzhou traffic bureau claimed to have reported reduced traffic problems and accidents in the downtown area since the ban.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guangzhou's main airport is the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Baiyun_International_Airport" title="Guangzhou Baiyun International Airport">Baiyun International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Huadu_District" title="Huadu District">Huadu District</a>; it opened on August 5, 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[143]</a></sup> This airport is the second busiest airport in terms of traffic movements in China. It replaced the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Baiyun_International_Airport_(former)" title="Guangzhou Baiyun International Airport (former)">old Baiyun International Airport</a>, which was very close to the city centre and failed to meet the city's fast-growing air traffic demand. The old Baiyun International Airport was in operation for 72 years.</p>
<p>Guangzhou Baiyun International Airport now has three runways, with two more planned.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[144]</a></sup> The Terminal 2 is under construction and will open in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou Station">Guangzhou Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_East_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou East Station">Guangzhou East Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_South_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou South Station">Guangzhou South Station</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_North_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou North Station">Guangzhou North Station</a></div>
<p>Guangzhou is the terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Guangzhou_Railway" title="Beijing–Guangzhou Railway">Beijing–Guangzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Shenzhen_Railway" title="Guangzhou–Shenzhen Railway">Guangzhou–Shenzhen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Maoming_Railway" title="Guangzhou–Maoming Railway">Guangzhou–Maoming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Meizhou%E2%80%93Shantou_Railway" title="Guangzhou–Meizhou–Shantou Railway">Guangzhou–Meizhou–Shantou</a> conventional speed railways. In late 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Wuhan%E2%80%93Guangzhou_High-Speed_Railway" title="Wuhan–Guangzhou High-Speed Railway">Wuhan–Guangzhou High-Speed Railway</a> started service, with <a href="/wiki/Multiple_unit" title="Multiple unit">multiple unit</a> trains covering 980&#160;km (608.94&#160;mi) at a top speed of 320&#160;km/h (199&#160;mph). In January 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Zhuhai_Intercity_Railway" title="Guangzhou–Zhuhai Intercity Railway">Guangzhou–Zhuhai Intercity Railway</a> started service at an average speed of 200&#160;km/h (124&#160;mph). In December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Guiyang%E2%80%93Guangzhou_High-Speed_Railway" title="Guiyang–Guangzhou High-Speed Railway">Guiyang–Guangzhou High-Speed Railway</a> and Nanning-Guangzhou Railway began service with trains running at top speeds of 250&#160;km/h (155&#160;mph) and 200&#160;km/h (124&#160;mph), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-SMD20141226_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMD20141226-154">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Through_Train_(MTR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangdong Through Train (MTR)">Guangdong Through Train</a> departs from the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_East_Railway_Station" title="Guangzhou East Railway Station">Guangzhou East railway station</a> and arrives at the <a href="/wiki/Hung_Hom_Station" title="Hung Hom Station">Hung Hom KCR station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kowloon" title="Kowloon">Kowloon, Hong Kong</a>. The route is approximately 182&#160;km (113&#160;mi) in length and the ride takes less than two hours. Frequent coach services are also provided with coaches departing every day from different locations (mostly major hotels) around the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_transport">Water transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Water transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are daily high-speed <a href="/wiki/Catamaran" title="Catamaran">catamaran</a> services between Nansha Ferry Terminal and Lianhua Shan Ferry Terminal in Guangzhou and the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_China_Ferry_Terminal" title="Hong Kong China Ferry Terminal">Hong Kong China Ferry Terminal</a>, as well as between Nansha Ferry Terminal and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_%E2%80%93_Macau_Ferry_Terminal,_Hong_Kong" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong – Macau Ferry Terminal, Hong Kong">Macau Ferry Pier</a> in Hong Kong.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>
</div>
<p>Within China, the <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese culture">culture</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">Cantonese people</a> is a subset of the larger "<a href="/wiki/Northern_and_southern_China" title="Northern and southern China">Southern</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Lingnan_culture" title="Lingnan culture">Lingnan</a>" cultural areas. Notable aspects of Guangzhou's cultural heritage include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangfu_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangfu dialect">Guangfu</a>, the local dialect of <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a></li>
<li>Yue or <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_cuisine" title="Cantonese cuisine">Cantonese cuisine</a>, one of China's eight major culinary traditions<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[n 9]</a></sup></li>
<li>Yue or <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_opera" title="Cantonese opera">Cantonese opera</a>, usually divided into martial and literary performances</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xiguan" title="Xiguan">Xiguan</a>, the area west of the former walled city</li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Opera_House" title="Guangzhou Opera House">Guangzhou Opera House</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Guangzhou Symphony Orchestra">Symphony Orchestra</a> also perform classical Western music and Chinese compositions in their style. <a href="/wiki/Guangdong_music_(genre)" title="Guangdong music (genre)">Cantonese music</a> is a style of traditional Chinese instrumental music, while <a href="/wiki/Cantopop" title="Cantopop">Cantopop</a> is the local form of <a href="/wiki/Rock-and-roll" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock-and-roll">rock-and-roll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop music</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing</a>-era Guangzhou had around 124 religious pavilions, halls, and temples.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837_32-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27EB.27.27187837-32">[32]</a></sup> Today, in addition to the Buddhist Association, Guangzhou also has a Taoist Association, a Jewish community,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[150]</a></sup> and a history with Christianity and Islam.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taoism">Taoism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Taoism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a> are still represented at a few of the city's temples. Among the most important is the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Five_Immortals_(Guangzhou)" title="Temple of the Five Immortals (Guangzhou)">Temple of the Five Immortals</a>, honoring the five <a href="/wiki/Taoist_immortals" class="mw-redirect" title="Taoist immortals">immortals</a> credited with introducing rice cultivation at the foundation of the city. The five rams they rode were supposed to have turned into stones upon their departure and gave the city several of its nicknames.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[151]</a></sup> Another place of worship is the <a href="/wiki/City_God_(China)" title="City God (China)">City God Temple</a>. Guangzhou, like most of southern China, is also notably observant concerning <a href="/wiki/Chinese_ancestral_veneration" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese ancestral veneration">ancestral veneration</a> during occasions like the <a href="/wiki/Tomb_Sweeping_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Tomb Sweeping Festival">Tomb Sweeping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghost_Festival" title="Ghost Festival">Ghost Festivals</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Buddhism">Buddhism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Buddhism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Buddhism" title="Chinese Buddhism">Buddhism</a> is the most prominent religion in Guangzhou.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[152]</a></sup> The Zhizhi Temple was founded in <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;233 from the estate of a <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Wu" title="Eastern Wu">Wu</a> official; it is said to comprise the residence of <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Jiande" title="Zhao Jiande">Zhao Jiande</a>, the last of the <a href="/wiki/Nanyue" title="Nanyue">Nanyue</a> <a href="/wiki/King_of_Nanyue" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Nanyue">kings</a>, and has been known as the <a href="/wiki/Guangxiao_Temple_(Guangzhou)" title="Guangxiao Temple (Guangzhou)">Guangxiao Temple</a> ("Temple of Bright Filial Piety") since the <a href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_missionary" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist missionary">missionary</a> <a href="/wiki/Bodhidharma" title="Bodhidharma">Bodhidharma</a> is traditionally said to have visited Panyu during the <a href="/wiki/Liu_Song_dynasty" title="Liu Song dynasty">Liu Song</a> or <a href="/wiki/Liang_dynasty" title="Liang dynasty">Liang</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_dynasties" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Chinese dynasties">dynasties</a> (5th or 6th century). Around <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;520, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Liang" title="Emperor Wu of Liang">Emperor Wu</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Liang_dynasty" title="Liang dynasty">Liang</a> ordered the construction of the Baozhuangyan Temple and the Xilai Monastery to store the relics of <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodian</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_saint" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist saint">Buddhist saints</a> which had been brought to the city and to house the monks beginning to assemble there. The Baozhuangyan is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Six_Banyan_Trees" title="Temple of the Six Banyan Trees">Temple of the Six Banyan Trees</a>, after a famous poem composed by <a href="/wiki/Su_Shi" title="Su Shi">Su Shi</a> after a visit during the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Song_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Song dynasty">Northern Song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[153]</a></sup> The Xilai Monastery was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Hualin_Temple" title="Hualin Temple">Hualin Temple</a> ("Flowery Forest Temple") after its reconstruction during the <a href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing</a>.</p>
<p>The temples were damaged by both the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republican</a> campaign to "Promote Education with Temple Property" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%BB%9F" class="extiw" title="wikt:廟">廟</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%94%A2" class="extiw" title="wikt:產">產</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%88%88" class="extiw" title="wikt:興">興</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%AD%B8" class="extiw" title="wikt:學">學</a></span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoist</a> <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> but have been renovated since the <a href="/wiki/Opening_up_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Opening up policy">opening up</a> that began in the 1980s. The Ocean Banner Temple on <a href="/wiki/Henan_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Henan Island">Henan Island</a>, once famous in the west as the only tourist spot in Guangzhou accessible to foreigners, has been reopened as the <a href="/wiki/Hoi_Tong_Monastery" title="Hoi Tong Monastery">Hoi Tong Monastery</a>.</p>

<p><span class="nowrap">The Hall of the 500 Arhats</span> at the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Flowery_Forest_Temple" class="mw-redirect" title="Flowery Forest Temple">Flowery Forest Temple</a></span> (Hualin) in the 1870s</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 132.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 132.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 130.66666666667px;">
<div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG/196px-Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG" width="131" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG/295px-Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG/394px-Hoi_Tong_Monastery_Pagoda.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The Thousand Buddha Tower at the present-day <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Hoi_Tong_Monastery" title="Hoi Tong Monastery">Hoi Tong Monastery</a></span></p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nestorianism" title="Nestorianism">Nestorian</a> <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_China" title="Christianity in China">Christians</a> first arrived in China via the overland <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, but suffered during <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wuzong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Wuzong of Tang">Emperor Wuzong</a>'s 845 <a href="/wiki/Great_Anti-Buddhist_Persecution" title="Great Anti-Buddhist Persecution">persecution</a> and were essentially extinct by the year 1000.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[154]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a>-era ban on foreigners limited <a href="/wiki/Christian_mission" title="Christian mission">missionaries</a> until it <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nanking" title="Treaty of Nanking">was abolished</a> following the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First Opium War</a>, although the <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_China" title="Protestantism in China">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morrison_(missionary)" title="Robert Morrison (missionary)">Robert Morrison</a> was able to perform some work through his service with the British factory. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Guangzhou" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Guangzhou">archdiocese</a> is housed at <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%27s_Sacred_Heart_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou's Sacred Heart Cathedral">Guangzhou's Sacred Heart Cathedral</a>, known locally as the "Stone House". A <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> edifice which was built by hand from 1861 to 1888 under <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">French</a> direction, its original Latin and French <a href="/wiki/Stained-glass_window" class="mw-redirect" title="Stained-glass window">stained-glass windows</a> were destroyed during the wars and amid the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>; they have since been replaced by English ones. The Canton Christian College (1888) and Hackett Medical College for Women (1902) were both founded by missionaries and now form part of Guangzhou's <a href="/wiki/Lingnan_University_(Guangzhou)" title="Lingnan University (Guangzhou)">Lingnan</a>. Since the opening up of China in the 1980s, there has been renewed interest in Christianity, but Guangzhou maintains pressure on underground churches which avoid registration with government officials.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[155]</a></sup> The Catholic archbishop <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Tang" title="Dominic Tang">Dominic Tang</a> was imprisoned without trial for 22 years, but his present successor is recognised by both the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a> and China's <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Patriotic_Catholic_Association" title="Chinese Patriotic Catholic Association">Patriotic Church</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Guangzhou has had a Muslim community since the earliest days of <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Islam</a>; the native or nativised adherents of the faith are known as the <a href="/wiki/Hui_people" title="Hui people">Hui</a>. <a href="/wiki/Huaisheng_Mosque" title="Huaisheng Mosque">Huaisheng Mosque</a> is one of the oldest extant <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> in the world, variously said to have been founded by the city's existing Arab community around the time of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>'s revelation or by Muhammad's visiting uncle in 627. <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">Muslims</a> sacked the city in 758<sup id="cite_ref-bret_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bret-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-welsh_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welsh-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-need_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-need-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sima_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sima-47">[46]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou massacre">were massacred</a> by the Chinese rebel <a href="/wiki/Huang_Chao" title="Huang Chao">Huang Chao</a> in 878, along with the <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in China">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christians_in_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Christians in China">Christians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-frenchy_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchy-48">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kaifung_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaifung-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gibberish_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gibberish-50">[49]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sirafi_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sirafi-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guy_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guy-52">[51]</a></sup> The Muslims who <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">martyred</a> themselves opposing the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Manchu</a> <a href="/wiki/Manchu_conquest_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchu conquest of China">conquest of the city</a> are still honored by a national monument at the tomb of "the Loyal Trio of Muslims".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27IDHP.27.271996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DvWLRxJEU49EC.26pg.3DPA306_306.5D_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27IDHP.27.271996.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DvWLRxJEU49EC.26pg.3DPA306_306.5D-165">[156]</a></sup> The modern city includes numerous <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Islamic_cuisine" title="Chinese Islamic cuisine">halal restaurants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG/200px-Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG/300px-Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG/400px-Stade_Olympique_Guangdong.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Olympic_Stadium" title="Guangdong Olympic Stadium">Guangdong Olympic Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tianhe_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Tianhe_Stadium.jpg/200px-Tianhe_Stadium.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Tianhe_Stadium.jpg/300px-Tianhe_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Tianhe_Stadium.jpg/400px-Tianhe_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tianhe_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tianhe_Stadium" title="Tianhe Stadium">Tianhe Stadium</a> is the home of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Evergrande" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou Evergrande">Guangzhou Evergrande</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 18,000 seat <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_International_Sports_Arena" title="Guangzhou International Sports Arena">Guangzhou International Sports Arena</a> will be one of the venues for the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIBA_Basketball_World_Cup" title="2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup">2019 FIBA Basketball World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 12–27 November 2010, Guangzhou hosted the <a href="/wiki/16th_Asian_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="16th Asian Games">16th Asian Games</a>. The same year, it hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Para_Games" title="2010 Asian Para Games">first Asian Para Games</a> from December 12 to 19. Combined, these were the largest sporting events the city ever hosted.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guangzhou also hosted the following major sporting events:</p>
<ul>
<li>1987 The 6th <a href="/wiki/National_Games_of_China" title="National Games of China">National Games of China</a></li>
<li>1991 The <a href="/wiki/1991_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="1991 FIFA Women's World Cup">1st FIFA Women's World Cup</a></li>
<li>2001 The <a href="/wiki/2001_National_Games_of_China" title="2001 National Games of China">2001 National Games of China</a></li>
<li>2007 The 8th National Traditional Games of Ethnic Minorities of the People's Republic of China</li>
<li>2008 The <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Team_Table_Tennis_Championships" title="2008 World Team Table Tennis Championships">49th World Table Tennis Championships</a></li>
<li>2009 The <a href="/wiki/2009_Sudirman_Cup" title="2009 Sudirman Cup">11th Sudirman Cup</a>: the world badminton mixed team championships</li>
</ul>
<p>Current professional sports clubs based in Guangzhou include:</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Evergrande_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou Evergrande FC">Guangzhou Evergrande FC</a> has risen in recent years to be a powerhouse in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> in the People's Republic of China, having won five consecutive <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_football_champions" title="List of Chinese football champions">national titles</a> in <a href="/wiki/2011_Chinese_Super_League" title="2011 Chinese Super League">2011</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Chinese_Super_League" title="2012 Chinese Super League">2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Chinese_Super_League" title="2013 Chinese Super League">2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_Chinese_Super_League" title="2014 Chinese Super League">2014</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Chinese_Super_League" title="2015 Chinese Super League">2015</a>. The team also won the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> in <a href="/wiki/2013_AFC_Champions_League" title="2013 AFC Champions League">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_AFC_Champions_League" title="2015 AFC Champions League">2015</a>. The club competed in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">2013 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, where it lost 3–0 in the semi-final stage to the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">2012–13 UEFA Champions League</a> winners <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eight_Views">Eight Views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Eight Views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eight_Views" title="Eight Views">Eight Views</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eight_Views_of_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="Eight Views of Guangzhou">Eight Views of Guangzhou</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eight_Views_of_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="Eight Views of Guangzhou">Eight Views of Ram City</a> are Guangzhou's eight most famous tourist attractions. They have varied over time since the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>, with some being named or demoted by emperors. The following modern list was chosen through public appraisal in 2011:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"Towers Shining through the <a href="/wiki/Zhujiang_New_Town" title="Zhujiang New Town">New Town</a>"</li>
<li>"The Pearl River Flowing and Shining": The <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(China)" title="Pearl River (China)">Pearl River</a> from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bai%27etan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bai'etan (page does not exist)">Bai'etan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Pazhou" title="Pazhou">Pazhou</a></li>
<li>"Cloudy Mountain Green and Tidy": <a href="/wiki/Baiyun_Mountain_Scenic_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Baiyun Mountain Scenic Area">Baiyun Mountain Scenic Area</a></li>
<li>"Yuexiu's Grandeur": <a href="/wiki/Yuexiu_Hill" title="Yuexiu Hill">Yuexiu Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuexiu_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuexiu Park">Park</a></li>
<li>"The Ancient Academy's Lingering Fame": The <a href="/wiki/Chen_Clan_Ancestral_Hall" title="Chen Clan Ancestral Hall">Chen Clan Ancestral Hall</a> and its folk art museum</li>
<li>"Liwan's Wonderful Scenery": <a href="/w/index.php?title=Liwan_Lake&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Liwan Lake (page does not exist)">Liwan Lake</a></li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Science_City" title="Guangzhou Science City">Science City</a>, Splendid as Brocade"</li>
<li>"Wetlands Singing at Night": <a href="/wiki/Nansha_Wetlands_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Nansha Wetlands Park">Nansha Wetlands Park</a></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_attractions">Tourist attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tourist attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guangzhou attracts more than 100 million visitors each year.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[162]</a></sup> There are many tourist attractions, including:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canton_Tower" title="Canton Tower">Canton Tower</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chen_Clan_Ancestral_Hall" title="Chen Clan Ancestral Hall">Chen Clan Ancestral Hall</a>, housing Guangzhou's folk art museum</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chime-Long_Paradise" class="mw-redirect" title="Chime-Long Paradise">Chime-Long Paradise</a></li>
<li>Chime-Long Waterpark (<span lang="zh-hans"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%95%BF" class="extiw" title="wikt:长">长</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%9A%86" class="extiw" title="wikt:隆">隆</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B0%B4" class="extiw" title="wikt:水">水</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%B8%8A" class="extiw" title="wikt:上">上</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E4%B9%90%E5%9B%AD" class="extiw" title="wikt:乐园">乐园</a></span>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Provincial_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangdong Provincial Museum">Guangdong Provincial Museum</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Zoo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guangzhou Zoo (page does not exist)">Guangzhou Zoo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huaisheng_Mosque" title="Huaisheng Mosque">Huaisheng Mosque</a>, site of the Plain Pagoda</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Mausoleum_of_the_Nanyue_King" title="Museum of the Mausoleum of the Nanyue King">Museum of the Mausoleum of the Nanyue King</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peasant_Movement_Training_Institute_at_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="Peasant Movement Training Institute at Guangzhou">Peasant Movement Training Institute</a>, an important Maoist site</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Cathedral_of_Guangzhou" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred Heart Cathedral of Guangzhou">Sacred Heart Cathedral</a> or Stone House</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangxiao_Temple_(Guangzhou)" title="Guangxiao Temple (Guangzhou)">Temple of Bright Filial Piety</a> (Guangxiao)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Six_Banyan_Trees" title="Temple of the Six Banyan Trees">Temple of the Six Banyan Trees</a> (Liurong), site of the Flowery Pagoda</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shamian_Island" title="Shamian Island">Shamian</a> or Shameen Island, the old trading compound</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall_(Guangzhou)" title="Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall (Guangzhou)">Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall</a>, site of Guangzhou's former presidential palace</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xiguan" title="Xiguan">Xiguan</a>, the western suburbs of the old city</li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Guangzhou has two local radio stations: the provincial <a href="/wiki/Radio_Guangdong" title="Radio Guangdong">Radio Guangdong</a> and the municipal <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Radio Guangzhou (page does not exist)">Radio Guangzhou</a>. Together they broadcast in more than a dozen channels. The primary language of both stations is <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>. Traditionally only one channel of Radio Guangdong is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin Chinese</a>. However, in recent years there has been an increase in Mandarin programmes on most Cantonese channels. Radio stations from cities around Guangzhou mainly broadcast in Cantonese and can be received in different parts of the city, depending on the radio stations' locations and transmission power. The Beijing-based <a href="/wiki/China_National_Radio" title="China National Radio">China National Radio</a> also broadcasts Mandarin programmes in the city. Radio Guangdong has a 30-minute weekly English programme, <i>Guangdong Today</i>, which is broadcast globally through the <a href="/wiki/WRN_Broadcast" title="WRN Broadcast">World Radio Network</a>. Daily English news programmes are also broadcast by Radio Guangdong.</p>
<p>Guangzhou has some of the best Chinese-language newspapers and magazines in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, most of which are published by three major newspaper groups in the city, the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Daily" title="Guangzhou Daily">Guangzhou Daily Press Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Daily" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Daily">Nanfang Press Corporation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Yangcheng_Evening_News" title="Yangcheng Evening News">Yangcheng Evening News Group</a>. The two leading newspapers of the city are <i><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Daily" title="Guangzhou Daily">Guangzhou Daily</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Southern_Metropolis_Daily" title="Southern Metropolis Daily">Southern Metropolis Daily</a></i>. The former, with a circulation of 1.8 million, has been China's most successful newspaper for 14 years in terms of advertising revenue, while <i>Southern Metropolis Daily</i> is considered one of the most liberal newspapers in mainland China. In addition to Guangzhou's Chinese-language publications, there are a few English magazines and newspapers. The most successful is <i>That's Guangzhou</i>, which started more than a decade ago and has since blossomed into <i><a href="/wiki/That%27s_PRD" title="That's PRD">That's PRD</a></i>, producing expatriate magazines in Beijing and Shanghai as well. It also produces <i>In the Red</i>.</p>
<p><span id="Guangzhou_Higher_Education_Mega_Centre"></span></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg/220px-North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg/330px-North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg/440px-North_Square_of_SYSU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3560" data-file-height="2248" /></a>

</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Higher_Education_Mega_Center" title="Guangzhou Higher Education Mega Center">Guangzhou Higher Education Mega Centre</a>, also known as Guangzhou University Town (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:广州">广州</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%A4%A7%E5%AD%A6" class="extiw" title="wikt:大学">大学</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9F%8E" class="extiw" title="wikt:城">城</a></span>), is a large tertiary education complex located in the southeast suburbs of Guangzhou. It occupies the entirety of <a href="/wiki/Xiaoguwei" title="Xiaoguwei">Xiaoguwei</a> Island in <a href="/wiki/Panyu_District" title="Panyu District">Panyu District</a>, covering an area of about 18 square kilometres (7&#160;sq&#160;mi). It houses new campuses from ten higher education institutions. The whole Higher Education Mega Centre can eventually accommodate up to 200,000 students, 20,000 teachers, and 50,000 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[163]</a></sup> The institutions include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Pharmaceutical_University" title="Guangdong Pharmaceutical University">Guangdong Pharmaceutical University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_University_of_Foreign_Studies" title="Guangdong University of Foreign Studies">Guangdong University of Foreign Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_University_of_Technology" title="Guangdong University of Technology">Guangdong University of Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Academy_of_Fine_Arts" title="Guangzhou Academy of Fine Arts">Guangzhou Academy of Fine Arts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_University" title="Guangzhou University">Guangzhou University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_University_of_Chinese_Medicine" title="Guangzhou University of Chinese Medicine">Guangzhou University of Chinese Medicine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_China_Normal_University" title="South China Normal University">South China Normal University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_China_University_of_Technology" title="South China University of Technology">South China University of Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_University" title="Sun Yat-sen University">Sun Yat-sen University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xinghai_Conservatory_of_Music" title="Xinghai Conservatory of Music">Xinghai Conservatory of Music</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Guangzhou's other fully accredited and degree-granting <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Guangdong" title="List of universities and colleges in Guangdong">universities and colleges</a> include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Guangdong Institute of Science and Technology">Guangdong Institute of Science and Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangdong_Polytechnic_Normal_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guangdong Polytechnic Normal University (page does not exist)">Guangdong Polytechnic Normal University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangdong_University_of_Finance_%26_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangdong University of Finance &amp; Economics">Guangdong University of Finance &amp; Economics</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangdong_University_of_Finance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guangdong University of Finance (page does not exist)">Guangdong University of Finance</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_College_of_South_China_University_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Guangzhou College of South China University of Technology (page does not exist)">Guangzhou College of South China University of Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Medical_University" title="Guangzhou Medical University">Guangzhou Medical University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Sports_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangzhou Sports University">Guangzhou Sports University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jinan_University" title="Jinan University">Jinan University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_China_Agricultural_University" title="South China Agricultural University">South China Agricultural University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Medical_University" title="Southern Medical University">Southern Medical University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhongkai_University_of_Agriculture_and_Engineering" title="Zhongkai University of Agriculture and Engineering">Zhongkai University of Agriculture and Engineering</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The two main comprehensive libraries are Guangzhou Library and Sun Yat-sen Library of Guangdong Province. <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Library" title="Guangzhou Library">Guangzhou Library</a> is a public library in Guangzhou. The library has moved to a new building in <a href="/wiki/Zhujiang_New_Town" title="Zhujiang New Town">Zhujiang New Town</a>, which fully opened on 23 June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[164]</a></sup> Sun Yat-sen Library of Guangdong Province has the largest collection of ancient books in Southern China.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Asia#China" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Asia">List of twin towns and sister cities in China</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twinnings_.E2.80.94_Sister_Cities">Twinnings — Sister Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Twinnings — Sister Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guangzhou currently maintains <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_China" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in China">sister city agreements</a> with 23 foreign cities.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[168]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Given in contemporary sources as the "Guisi Day" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%99%B8%E5%B7%B3" class="extiw" title="wikt:癸巳">癸巳</a></span>) of the 9th <a href="/wiki/Chinese_calendar" title="Chinese calendar">lunar month</a> of the first year of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_era_name" title="Chinese era name">Qianyuan Era</a> under <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Suzong_of_Tang" title="Emperor Suzong of Tang">Emperor Suzong</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The term "Persian" may, however, have been loosely applied and referred indifferently to any similar-looking foreign women.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-69">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"<a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_China" title="Slavery in China">Buying and selling of children</a> was scarcely unknown in Ming China, but the large new demands of the Portuguese may have stimulated kidnappings from good families..."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWills_.26_al.2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DzERymZzBQQYC.26pg.3DPA28_28.5D_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWills_.26_al.2010.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DzERymZzBQQYC.26pg.3DPA28_28.5D-68">[66]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Some early Chinese historians go even so far as to give vivid details of the price paid for the children and how they were roasted."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR39_xxxix.5D_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECortesao1944.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.com.2Fbooks.3Fid.3Dh82D-Y0E3TwC.26pg.3DPR39_xxxix.5D-74">[71]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"On the day of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">St Nicholas</a> [6 Dec.] in the year 1522 they put <a href="/wiki/Cangue" title="Cangue">boards</a> on them with the sentence that they should die and be exposed in <a href="/wiki/Cangue" title="Cangue">pillories</a> as <a href="/wiki/Wokou" title="Wokou">robbers</a>. The sentences said: 'Petty <a href="/wiki/Wokou" title="Wokou">sea robbers</a> sent by the great robber falsely; they come to spy out our country; let them die in <a href="/wiki/Cangue" title="Cangue">pillories</a> as <a href="/wiki/Wokou" title="Wokou">robbers</a>.' A report was sent to <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_Emperor" title="Jiajing Emperor">the king</a> according to the information of the <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_(official)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandarin (official)">mandarins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jiajing_Emperor" title="Jiajing Emperor">the king</a> confirmed the sentence. On 23 Sept. 1523 these twenty-three persons were each one <a href="/wiki/Lingchi" title="Lingchi">cut in pieces</a>, to wit, heads, legs, arms, and their <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_organs#Male" class="mw-redirect" title="Reproductive organs">private members</a> placed in their mouths, the trunk of the body being divided into two pieces round the belly. In the streets of Canton, outside the walls, in the suburbs, through the principal streets they were put to death, at distances of one crossbow shot from one another, that all might see them, both those of Canton and those of the environs, in order to give them to understand that they thought nothing of the Portuguese, so that the people might not talk of the Portuguese. Thus... they were all killed, and their heads and <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_organs#male" class="mw-redirect" title="Reproductive organs">private members</a> were carried on the backs of the Portuguese in front of the <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_(official)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandarin (official)">mandarins</a> of Canton with the playing of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_musical_instruments" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese musical instruments">musical instruments</a> and rejoicing, were exhibited suspended in the streets, and were then thrown into the <a href="/wiki/Dunghill" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunghill">dunghills</a>. And from henceforth it was resolved not to allow any more Portuguese into the country nor other strangers."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Shaowu Emperor's remains are buried in <a href="/wiki/Yuexiu_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuexiu Park">Yuexiu Park</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In fact, the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Asiatic_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Asiatic Company">Danish Asiatic Company</a> was formally chartered in April 1732 while this first ship, the <i><span lang="da">Cron-Printz Christian</span></i>, was on its return trip.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[87]</a></sup> Counting the <i>Cron-Printz Christian</i>, up to 1833, the DAC dispatched 130 ships to Guangzhou, losing five. The average voyage from <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> took 216 days and the voyage back, 192.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunn.5Bhttps:.2F.2Fbooks.google.co.jp.2Fbooks.3Fid.3DE10tnvapZt0C.26pg.3DPA208_208.5D-90">[84]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The statement is an excerpt from the longer proverb "Be born in <a href="/wiki/Suzhou" title="Suzhou">Suzhou</a>, play in <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou" title="Hangzhou">Hangzhou</a>, eat in Guangzhou, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_funeral_rituals" title="Chinese funeral rituals">die</a> in <a href="/wiki/Liuzhou" title="Liuzhou">Liuzhou</a>" (<span lang="zh"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%94%9F" class="extiw" title="wikt:生">生</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:在">在</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E8%8B%8F%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:苏州">苏州</a>，<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E7%8E%A9" class="extiw" title="wikt:玩">玩</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:在">在</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9D%AD%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:杭州">杭州</a>，<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E9%A3%9F" class="extiw" title="wikt:食">食</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:在">在</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%B9%BF%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:广州">广州</a>，<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%AD%BB" class="extiw" title="wikt:死">死</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E5%9C%A8" class="extiw" title="wikt:在">在</a><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%9F%B3%E5%B7%9E" class="extiw" title="wikt:柳州">柳州</a></span>).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The other seven are the cuisines of <a href="/wiki/Anhui_cuisine" title="Anhui cuisine">Anhui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fujian_cuisine" title="Fujian cuisine">Fujian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunan_cuisine" title="Hunan cuisine">Hunan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu_cuisine" title="Jiangsu cuisine">Jiangsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shandong_cuisine" title="Shandong cuisine">Shandong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sichuan_cuisine" title="Sichuan cuisine">Sichuan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_cuisine" title="Zhejiang cuisine">Zhejiang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beautyfujian_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beautyfujian-156">[148]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">

<table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br />
<p><sup>a</sup><a href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>. <sup>b</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>. <sup>c</sup><a href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-provincial city in the People's Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>. <sup>1</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>. <sup>2</sup><a href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br />
<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br />
<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br />
<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People's Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. See <a href="/wiki/Template:Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China">Template:Administrative divisions of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br /></p>
All provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by province.</div>

<div>
